    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1275317195">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1275317195" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy" class="left imgcol" title="Ferdy"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1402844429p2/4596358.jpg" alt="Ferdy" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1275317195?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 07, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy" class="user" title="Ferdy">Ferdy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/17718086-a-tree-grows-in-brooklyn" title="Paperback 9780062096951" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=likeable-heroine" class="actionLinkLite">likeable-heroine</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=classic" class="actionLinkLite">classic</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=engrossing" class="actionLinkLite">engrossing</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=loved-it" class="actionLinkLite">loved-it</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=loved-the-setting" class="actionLinkLite">loved-the-setting</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=coming-of-age" class="actionLinkLite">coming-of-age</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1275317195">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4830801710923081807"><strong>Spoilers</strong><br /><br />I wasn't expecting to love this as much as I did, despite all the darker themes it contained, it still somehow managed to be a lovely, warm and charming read. <br /><br />-I enjoyed how the story was less plot driven and more focused on the characters. I loved reading about Francie Nolan and her family, and all the struggles and ups and downs they faced and how it made them change and grow over the years. I didn't expect to be so engrossed by all the grim and ordinary details of their day to day to</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4830801710923081807"><strong>Spoilers</strong><br /><br />I wasn't expecting to love this as much as I did, despite all the darker themes it contained, it still somehow managed to be a lovely, warm and charming read. <br /><br />-I enjoyed how the story was less plot driven and more focused on the characters. I loved reading about Francie Nolan and her family, and all the struggles and ups and downs they faced and how it made them change and grow over the years. I didn't expect to be so engrossed by all the grim and ordinary details of their day to day to lives, but it was just so easy to immerse into.<br /><br />-The 1900s Brooklyn setting was written really well, at times Francie's description of her neighbourhood read as quite magical and surreal - the atmosphere and visuals were just described so vividly. <br /><br />-I pretty much loved every single character. Even the ones I hated I still managed to love for how well crafted and flawed and realistic they were (especially Francie's parents, Johnny and Katie). <br /><br />-Francie was a great narrator, all her observations and thoughts were wonderful to read. Her various routines in Brooklyn never failed to fascinate, even when she was buying bread or meat, getting books from the library, attending school or reading on the fire escape. Those simple and everyday sorts of things were somehow utterly engrossing to read. <br /><br />-Francie wasn't without her flaws, I had major issues with her attitude towards females, any time a woman/girl or a group of women/girls would disappoint her in some way or another, she would write off all women/girls as bad and awful. It never crossed her mind that she was wrong to condemn all women for the actions of a few, in her mind if a few were bad, they all were. And then there was Francie complaining about not having any friends, she never once thought that maybe she was the problem. She rarely made any sort of effort with anyone at school or work, she always kept to herself and acted cold. What did she think would happen? Who wants to be friends with someone like that? I swear Franice was so dense sometimes.<br />Despite the many irritating facets of Francie's personality, I still adored her and thought she was a great protagonist.<br /><br />-The whole Ben/Lee drama was kind of odd. Francie had known Ben for months, they helped each other and were friends and had feelings for one another, their relationship was organic and made sense and fit Francie's personality. But then out of nowhere she fell madly in love with Lee when she'd known him for less than two days and had spent less than 12 hours with him. Where the hell did that come from?! She didn't even know him but that didn't stop her from claiming her undying love for him. I know she was only sixteen and knew nothing about romance and relationships, but I still expected more from her. <br />I suppose she needed the whole whirlwind mini-romance with Lee so she could learn from that and be more realistic and grounded when it came to her relationship with Ben. But even with that the whole Lee arc was still kind of dumb.<br /><br />-I despised Francie's mum, she was such an infuriating character. Even though she had all the ingredients of being a strong and likeable woman and had a no-nonsense, hard working, dedicated attitude, I just couldn't stand her. Most of the time she came across as a holier-than-thou, poisonous, hateful cow. I think my hatred of her stemmed from how she treated her kids, she felt such love for her son (Neelie) and such indifference for Francie. She loved Neelie because he was a strong, healthy boy yet felt contempt for Francie as she was a sickly baby girl. Any loving feeling Katie had for Francie was down to pity and obligation. I didn't get it, Francie was just as much her child as Neelie, and if anything Franice needed her far more than Neelie. It wasn't even favouritism, she loved one and disliked the other. Francie may as well have been a stranger considering how little Katie felt for her. Katie's epic love for one child and coldness to another was plain fucked up. What was even worse was Katie complaining that Francie and her weren't close and didn't understand each other whereas her and Neelie had a special bond. Did it not occur to her that the only reason Francie wasn't close to her was because she'd more or less been rejected by her? Katie showered all her love and attention on Neelie and gave nothing to Francie, it was no wonder Francie was left hurt by that and turned to her dad for some basic parental affection. <br />Then there was Katie's attitude towards other women, she was so harsh and bitchy (even worse than Franice). It was hard to like Katie even with all the burdens she had to carry and the back breaking work she had to do when her coldness and viciousness about Francie and other women would rear its ugly head every few pages. Even though Katie had suffered so much loss and heartache, I hated that she managed to get a happy ending. I didn't feel like she deserved it when she made it clear that Francie meant so little her. How horrible for a child to grow up knowing that their sibling was so loved by their mother whilst they were seen as nothing but a nuisance. Ugh, hated Katie so much for treating Francie like crap.<br /><br />-I found Johnny far more easier to like and sympathise with than Katie despite him being a cheating, irresponsible, weak, drunk loser. At least he didn't favour one of his children over the other and managed to show both his kids warmth and love when he never wanted to be a dad in the first place. I wasn't expecting him to even stick around in his marriage after Katie gave birth, but he did and in his own way he tried to be a good dad and husband. Sure, he failed spectacularly and kept losing his jobs and getting drunk, but it did seem like he genuinely tried his best. I felt nothing but pity for his constant failure and alcoholism, he only turned to drink when things got too much for him and when he was lost and depressed. I wasn't surprised he was the way he was when he got little emotional support and kindness from Katie. His drinking only got worse the more she nagged and ignored him, the poor guy didn't stand a chance with such a cold, stuck up cow.<br />His death was quite depressing to read, he didn't deserve to die in such a lonely and pathetic way, especially when it felt like he was crying out for help and support. He would have been better off leaving Katie and the kids and moving back in with his mum so she could look after him and help him get back on his feet.<br /><br />-Sissy was the absolute best character by far, I think she's one of my all time favourite fictional characters ever. She was so compassionate, open minded, strong, and helpful, all whilst being fun and flawed and interesting. It was so easy to root for her when she was so honest and upbeat despite suffering and losing so much. In a lot of ways she was on top, but when it came down to it she was a bit of an underdog in life, nothing that she really wanted ever worked out for her (well, until the very end).<br />Her relationship with Francie was great, she was more of a mother to her than Katie was. I was sure Sissy would have a go at for Katie for being such a rubbish mum and taking Francie for granted, but sadly that didn't happen. Ugh, I really wanted someone to put Katie in her place.<br />I loved the parts where Sissy called all her fellas 'John', and when she pretended to have a baby and drove her husband crazy with her fake pregnancy/birth. Also, the part where Sissy put Francie's awful teacher in her place was great, they were all such hilarious and brilliant moments.<br /><br />-I don't know why but <em>A Tree Grows in Brooklyn</em> felt really homey and comforting despite so much of it being foreign and unfamiliar. I suppose a lot of the daily struggle, family life, and growing pains were familiar enough though, and those elements were at the heart of the book, and were easy to relate to. <br /><br />-The darker themes (alcoholism, poverty, death, perverts, misogyny) were interwoven into the story really well, none of them seemed out of place or done for shock value or drama or preachy purposes. It all felt very organic and fit in with the quieter and lighter aspects of the book.<br /><br />I can see why <em>A Tree Grows in Brooklyn</em> is a classic, it's brilliant. <br />Highly recommended for those who love coming-of-age stories with lots of focus on family drama and day-to-day life.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4830801710923081807">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_9722064">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/9722064" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/647547-mariel" class="left imgcol" title="Mariel"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1451321467p2/647547.jpg" alt="Mariel" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/9722064?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 15, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/647547-mariel" class="user" title="Mariel">Mariel</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/14891.A_Tree_Grows_in_Brooklyn" title="Paperback 9780061120077" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone with a heart</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Mariel by: </span>
      young me found it by sheer luck
  </div>



    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer9722064">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7840562402056946513">I read A Tree Grows In Brooklyn when I was about fourteen years of age. I've not reread it since, so this is more of a review of the value of the long lasting impression it made on me in my formative years (although I believe all of my years are formative ones).<br /><br />Betty Smith's novel is in some ways autobiographical. If not, there are parallels in a cracked two-way mirror kinda way. I imagine the author would peer through the holes onto the other side and recognize Betty Smith.<br /><br />There are parts of th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7840562402056946513">I read A Tree Grows In Brooklyn when I was about fourteen years of age. I've not reread it since, so this is more of a review of the value of the long lasting impression it made on me in my formative years (although I believe all of my years are formative ones).<br /><br />Betty Smith's novel is in some ways autobiographical. If not, there are parallels in a cracked two-way mirror kinda way. I imagine the author would peer through the holes onto the other side and recognize Betty Smith.<br /><br />There are parts of the story about how young Francie discovers the desire in herself to become a writer. I know, this is a pretty big cliche in stories about young characters written by adults who became writers. A sort of "I did it!" nostalgic looksie. (Most teen shows feature at least one callow "writer" who drops the notion at the drop of a hat.) A Tree Grows In Brooklyn is not that tale. Betty Smith is not that self-obsessed person writing about being a writer as if that was the point at all. What I found so special about this book was the feeling that Francie was taking my hand and inviting me to spend some time with her in her life. I got to look into that mirror too. Know me, not look at me.<br /><br />Even though I haven't read this in some years, I remember things as if it happened to me yesterday. Have you ever felt that things can get you down so much so why even bother? Anyway, those early teen years were pretty hard. A Tree Grows In Brooklyn was like a "Everything is going to be okay" that I could actually believe. I believed Francie when she thinks that they were lucky that they had what they did have. Some people's happiness comes off fake and full of shit. Hers didn't because Smith was too good at putting the reader in that life with them. Smith and Francie knew from the inside how to look at it. You can't blind yourself to either the good or the bad.<br /><br />It still makes me unbearably sad about Francie's mom, how she loved her son more because he wasn't tough like Francie had to be. Sometimes one's feelings about oneself can affect how we feel about our loved ones in a bad way. It's good to see this from someone else's eyes, lest you take it for granted your own deficiencies are at fault. My teen self could relate too well having a mother who loves my brother more than she could ever be capable of loving me. Some things are a sad fact of life that we cannot change. I've also had people like her father in my family: fun, but utterly and tragically unreliable. Seeing them for what they really are can be a necessary wake-up call. If you don't, you'll never be able to love them for who they really are, and it goes on hurting you forever.<br /><br />The classic film from 1945 is really good. Not a patch on the book, however. It has a kabuki emotional feel to it, meaning it was too self conscious about taking the audience through path a to path b. The book feels real like you lived it. I forgot my own woes in the company of someone else's. That is much better than wallowing, to my mind. The movie you just watch. If you've only seen the movie, please read the book and recognize. (I'm not saying all movies are less intimate than books, just this one. There's a certain quality about old movies, I don't know what it is. Maybe because they were trained to all speak the same way?)</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7840562402056946513">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1428166162">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1428166162" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/30704264-beth" class="left imgcol" title="Beth"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1431715222p2/30704264.jpg" alt="Beth" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1428166162?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 29, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/30704264-beth" class="user" title="Beth">Beth</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/12200015-a-tree-grows-in-brooklyn" title="Mass Market Paperback " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/30704264-beth?shelf=coming-of-age" class="actionLinkLite">coming-of-age</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/30704264-beth?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/30704264-beth?shelf=e-books-from-library" class="actionLinkLite">e-books-from-library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1428166162">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9496786993555838771">Sigh, this will always be my favorite book.<br /><br />My childhood copy has been loved and re-read many many times -- I was afraid it wouldn't hold up to another re-read so I was pleasantly surprised to discover that <a rel="nofollow" href="https://openlibrary.org/">Open Library</a> had an e-book version I could borrow. I think I was on the wait list for about two months -- and then just as I finished a book, the angels sang, and I got an e-mail notification that it was my turn -- oh I love it when things work out that way!<br /><br /><em>A Tree Grows in Brooklyn</em> was just as</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9496786993555838771">Sigh, this will always be my favorite book.<br /><br />My childhood copy has been loved and re-read many many times -- I was afraid it wouldn't hold up to another re-read so I was pleasantly surprised to discover that <a rel="nofollow" href="https://openlibrary.org/">Open Library</a> had an e-book version I could borrow. I think I was on the wait list for about two months -- and then just as I finished a book, the angels sang, and I got an e-mail notification that it was my turn -- oh I love it when things work out that way!<br /><br /><em>A Tree Grows in Brooklyn</em> was just as wonderful as I remembered. And I have to say, it is an immense relief. Honestly, I really don't who I would be anymore if I didn't love this book. I have loved this book since when I first read it -- I'm guessing I was maybe 13 years old at the time.<br /><br />And I don't want to come across as ungrateful but this borrowed e-book had a lot of typos (or better put, formatting issues) -- I'm confident the actual print edition does not. I haven't experienced e-book typos/formatting issues like this before -- the e-books that I borrow from the library and the free public domain ones I've downloaded from <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.feedbooks.com/">feedbooks</a> have always been just fine.<br /><br />Some of the formatting issues were minor, little things like "<strong>m</strong>" instead of "<strong>in</strong>" or "<strong>d</strong>" instead of "<strong>cl</strong>." But then there was really weird stuff like this:<blockquote>
<br />"Kate frowned and Francie dropped the <strong>sul&gt;i(*t</strong>." (That word should be "subject.") And this one: "She put <strong>lier lieaci</strong> down on <strong>iljc</strong> table and wept." (I'm pretty sure that should be "She put her letter down on the table and wept.")</blockquote> <br /><br />Still, odd formatting aside, it really did not detract from me enjoying my read. I still love, and will always love, <em>A Tree Grows in Brooklyn</em>. <br /><br />read from October 22, 2015 - October 28, 2015</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9496786993555838771">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_221352525">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/221352525" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6610433-midnightfaerie" class="left imgcol" title="midnightfaerie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1318372863p2/6610433.jpg" alt="midnightfaerie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/221352525?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 16, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6610433-midnightfaerie" class="user" title="midnightfaerie">midnightfaerie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/14891.A_Tree_Grows_in_Brooklyn" title="Paperback 9780061120077" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6610433-midnightfaerie?shelf=literature" class="actionLinkLite">literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer221352525">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15891313484813990636">A Tree Grows in Brooklyn by Betty Smith is an amazing story of a girl coming of age in the 1900's. She lives in the poor part of Brooklyn and tells the story of her life growing up, learning to deal with harsh realities and still finding the wonder in life and holding onto it. Smith is a brilliant writer. Her depiction of reality in such a precarious time is both insightful and a joy to read. You are drawn into Francie's story, the disappointments in life, the sadness, and the wonderful viewpoin</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15891313484813990636">A Tree Grows in Brooklyn by Betty Smith is an amazing story of a girl coming of age in the 1900's. She lives in the poor part of Brooklyn and tells the story of her life growing up, learning to deal with harsh realities and still finding the wonder in life and holding onto it. Smith is a brilliant writer. Her depiction of reality in such a precarious time is both insightful and a joy to read. You are drawn into Francie's story, the disappointments in life, the sadness, and the wonderful viewpoint of a child writer. Francie's parents, like so many others, were immigrants, coming to America to want for a better life for her children. When Francie's mother asks her Grandmother advice on how to accomplish this dream she replies by telling her to start a savings, making sure you own a piece of land before you die. Also, to read to the children each night a page from Shakespeare and a page from the Bible. And to tell them stories of elves and fairies and such. Her mother replies that won't that just disappoint them later? And the grandmother replies, no, that it's needed to fatten up their imaginations so that when sad things happen to them, then can fall back on those imaginations to get them through. Smith states it so much more elegantly than I've remembered here but there were so many of these elegant tidbits, I had to try and relate one here. Overall an excellent read and definitely in its own class of books. <br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://classicsdefined.com/tree.html"> ClassicsDefined.com</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15891313484813990636">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_141683873">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/141683873" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/619633-uci" class="left imgcol" title="Uci "><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1356222737p2/619633.jpg" alt="Uci " /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/141683873?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 08, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/619633-uci" class="user" title="Uci ">Uci </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/10040773-sebatang-pohon-tumbuh-di-brooklyn" title="Paperback 9789792264920" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/619633-uci?shelf=pinjaman-tanpa-bunga" class="actionLinkLite">pinjaman-tanpa-bunga</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer141683873">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9989518551407134566">Saya sempat bertanya-tanya mengapa harus ada kata pengantar dari Anne Quindlen (novelis, jurnalis dan kolumnis AS) untuk novel ini. Namun setelah membacanya, saya rasa novel yang awalnya dibuat sebagai memoar ini memang layak diberi catatan khusus. Pembaca yang mengharapkan plot atau konflik seru mungkin harus menelan kecewa, karena novel ini, seperti lazimnya sebuah memoar, 'hanya' bercerita tentang perjalanan hidup, bukan ledakan-ledakan peristiwa yang membuat pembaca ikut pontang-panting. <br /><br />Nam</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9989518551407134566">Saya sempat bertanya-tanya mengapa harus ada kata pengantar dari Anne Quindlen (novelis, jurnalis dan kolumnis AS) untuk novel ini. Namun setelah membacanya, saya rasa novel yang awalnya dibuat sebagai memoar ini memang layak diberi catatan khusus. Pembaca yang mengharapkan plot atau konflik seru mungkin harus menelan kecewa, karena novel ini, seperti lazimnya sebuah memoar, 'hanya' bercerita tentang perjalanan hidup, bukan ledakan-ledakan peristiwa yang membuat pembaca ikut pontang-panting. <br /><br />Namun, ungkapan "reality is larger than fiction" memang bukan sekadar omong kosong. Dalam novel ini kita mengikuti perjalanan seorang gadis bernama Francie Nolan, putri dari pasangan imigran Polandia-Irlandia, yang mencari kehidupan lebih baik di Amerika, tepatnya di Brooklyn. Dengan setting waktu di awal tahun 1900-an, detail-detail perjuangan para imigran digambarkan dengan sangat menarik oleh Betty Smith. Kemiskinan, kekerasan, pelecehan dan kebodohan menjadi kenyataan hidup sehari-hari dan Francie berhasil keluar dari kubangan gelap itu dengan pendidikan serta tekad baja. <em>Harus ada genangan air yang gelap dan berlumpur supaya matahari memiliki latar untuk membiaskan kilau megahnya.</em><br /><br />Orangtua Francie sendiri sangat bertolak belakang, meski awalnya disatukan oleh cinta buta saat mereka masih belia. <em>Katie memiliki keinginan kuat untuk bertahan hidup dan itu membuatnya jadi pejuang. Johnny selalu berharap bisa hidup selamanya dan itu membuatnya jadi tukang khayal tak berguna.</em> Terbukti, ayahnya yang pemabuk pergi lebih dulu meninggalkan Francie, adiknya Neely, dan istri yang tengah mengandung anak ketiga. Berempat, mereka mengarungi kerasnya kehidupan di Brooklyn.<br /><br />Namun, jangan mengira buku ini penuh adegan mengharukan yang membuat hati trenyuh. Kemiskinan di sini tidak digambarkan sebagai sesuatu yang harus ditangisi, tapi dilawan. Francie yang selalu kesepian menemukan hiburan dengan membaca buku di perpustakaan, walaupun selama bertahun-tahun meminjam buku di sana, sang pustakawan tak pernah sekalipun mengangkat muka untuk memandangnya. <br /><br />Kecerdasan Francie membuatnya menonjol di sekolah, dan kegemarannya menulis mulai terasah. Walaupun sekali lagi dia harus menelan kecewa karena gurunya memberi nilai jelek setiap kali dia menulis tentang kenyataan. <em>"Kemiskinan, kelaparan dan mabuk-mabuk adalah topik yang tidak baik. Kita semua tahu hal-hal itu ada. Tapi orang tidak menulis tentang itu semua."</em><br /><br />Francie mulai paham bahwa kehidupannya mungkin menjijikkan di mata orang berpendidikan. Maka, dengan caranya sendiri, Francie menjalani kehidupan seraya berjuang untuk menjadi 'seseorang', tidak lagi menjadi gadis miskin yang hina. <br /><br />Begitu banyak kutipan bagus yang saya dapat dari novel setebal 600-an halaman ini. Rasanya akan terlalu panjang jika saya tuliskan semuanya. Pengamatan Francie terhadap lingkungan sekitar, interaksi dengan keluarga serta tetangga dan teman, memberi banyak hal untuk direnungkan. Salah satunya tentang kekejaman ibu-ibu di lingkungannya, yang menghakimi dan menggunjingkan seorang gadis yang punya anak di luar nikah. Padahal Francie tahu ibu-ibu itu hidup dalam kemunafikan: punya suami tapi tidak bahagia, kehidupan mereka hanya diisi dengan pertengkaran dan kebencian. <em>Kebanyakan wanita punya satu persamaan: mereka merasakan sakit luar biasa saat melahirkan. Seharusnya ini menjadi pengikat yang menyatukan mereka semua; seharusnya mereka menyayangi dan melindungi satu sama lain di dunia-pria. Tapi tidak demikian. Rupanya sakit melahirkan yang luar biasa telah menciutkan hati dan jiwa mereka. Mereka hanya bersatu untuk satu hal: untuk menyerang wanita lain...entah dengan melempar batu atau dengan gosip kejam. Sepertinya itulah satu-satunya kesetiaan yang mereka miliki.</em><br /><br />Dari mata polos Francie, kita juga bisa melihat ulah licik para politisi yang sepertinya tak pernah berubah sampai sekarang. Mereka membodohi warga miskin dengan iming-iming makanan dan uang agar terus memilih mereka, dengan janji-janji surga yang tak pernah diwujudkan, tak peduli selama apa mereka duduk di bangku kekuasaan.<br /><br />Intinya, novel ini bercerita tentang kehidupan. Dan pelajaran apa yang bisa lebih besar dari pelajaran hidup? Setelah menutup halaman terakhir, saya sempat terdiam dan merenung betapa indah kehidupan jika kita bisa melihatnya dengan mata yang jernih dan jiwa yang tak kenal menyerah. Betty Smith, yang bernama asli Elisabeth Wehner, menuturkan dengan gamblang dalam kata penutupnya yang turut dicantumkan dalam novel ini: <em>Aku pun sampai pada suatu kesimpulan yang jelas dan universal: Hidup, berjuang, jatuh cinta pada hidup - jatuh cinta pada segala hal dalam hidup, kesenangan atau kesedihan - itulah kepuasan. Kepuasan hidup terbuka bagi kita semua.</em><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9989518551407134566">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/393599894?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 04, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4776032-cher" class="user" title="Cher">Cher</a>

        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer393599894">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12164399661229984622"><strong>3 stars - It was good.</strong><br /><br />After hearing from so many of my friends that this was an endearing, well-loved, favorite classic, I'm afraid it did not meet my expectations. I really enjoyed the first half, particularly when the author gives you the back story of the main character's grandparents and parents, but the second half felt like a chore to get through at times (making me want to 23 skidoo). There are beautiful quotes throughout and I enjoyed the author's way with words, but the plot needed more</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12164399661229984622"><strong>3 stars - It was good.</strong><br /><br />After hearing from so many of my friends that this was an endearing, well-loved, favorite classic, I'm afraid it did not meet my expectations. I really enjoyed the first half, particularly when the author gives you the back story of the main character's grandparents and parents, but the second half felt like a chore to get through at times (making me want to 23 skidoo). There are beautiful quotes throughout and I enjoyed the author's way with words, but the plot needed more oomph to keep me engaged. The most enjoyable components of the novel were the characterization and the literary visit to the turn of the century. <br />-------------------------------------------<br /><strong>Favorite Quote:</strong> From that moment on, the world was hers for the reading. She would never be lonely again.<br /><br /><strong>First Sentence:</strong> Serene was a word you could put to Brooklyn, New York. <br /></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('C99PGuEU90CbATwUy9g4eGwsIH+6vGyyknkiIw0MgtJuC3DJE8bjuhfZSK+1ud7KJdvjZvNhKxj4cCexwZl0lw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {

    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

From Granpa he absorbed th&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;span id=\"freeText2846857310476153635\" style=\"display:none\"&gt;Forrest Carter, from the age of four or five, was inseparable from his part-Cherokee grandfather, who owned a farm and ran a country store nearby. Granpa called him Little Sprout; when he grew taller, he became Little Tree. From Granpa he absorbed the Cherokee ethic; to give love without expecting gratitude, to take from the land only what you need. Little Tree watches a mountain storm when Nature is birthing Spring, learns bird signs and wind songs and which crops to plant by the dark of the moon. He hears the true story of the Cherokee Trail of Tears, and why it is not the Indian who wept, but the watching white man. From a Jewish peddler who came every season to Granpa\'s store he learns a lesson in charity; from a sharecropper he learns to understand misplaced pride. He escapes death through Granpa\'s courage and confronts, for the first time, the hypocrisy and brutality of white Americans.Much of the lore passed from generation to generation by word of mouth is found in these stories in &amp;quot;The Education of Little Tree,&amp;quot; autobiographical if not all factually accurate. For instance, Granma is based on family memories of Carter\'s great-great-great grandmother (Granpa\'s great-grandmother), who was a full Cherokee, combined with the author\'s own mother, who read Shakespeare to him when he was a child. But Granpa is all and forever true in this storyteller\'s memoir of a time that ended when Little Tree was ten and Granpa died.&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;a data-text-id=\"2846857310476153635\" href=\"#\" Take, for example, Shoba and Shukumar, the young couple in &amp;quot;A Temporary Matter&amp;quot; whose marriage is crumbling in the wake of a stillborn child. Or Miranda in &amp;quot;Sexy,&amp;quot; who is involved in a hopeless affair with a married man. But Mr. Kapasi has problems enough of his own; in addition to his regular job working as an interpreter for a doctor who does not speak his patients\' language, he also drives tourists to local sites of interest. His fare on this particular day is Mr. and Mrs. Das--first-generation Americans of Indian descent--and their children. During the course of the afternoon, Mr. Kapasi becomes enamored of Mrs. Das and then becomes her unwilling confidant when she reads too much into his profession. &amp;quot;I told you because of your talents,&amp;quot; she informs him after divulging a startling secret.  I\'m tired of feeling so terrible all the time. Eight years, Mr. Kapasi, I\'ve been in pain eight years. I was hoping you could help me feel better; say the right thing. Suggest some kind of remedy.  Of course, Mr. Kapasi has no cure for what ails Mrs. Das--or himself. Lahiri\'s subtle, bittersweet ending is characteristic of the collection as a whole. Some of these nine tales are set in India, others in the United States, and most concern characters of Indian heritage. Yet the situations Lahiri\'s people face, from unhappy marriages to civil war, transcend ethnicity. As the narrator of the last story, &amp;quot;The Third and Final Continent,&amp;quot; comments: &amp;quot;There are times I am bewildered by each mile I have traveled, each meal I have eaten, each person I have known, each room in which I have slept.&amp;quot; In that single line Jhumpa Lahiri sums up a universal experience, one that applies to all who have grown up, left home, fallen in or out     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/2327917.Betty_Smith">About Betty  Smith</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/2327917.Betty_Smith"><img alt="2327917" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1238556081p2/2327917.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer10891537771033427862"><em>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name. <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/44217-master-list-of-author-disambiguation-by-spaces">See this thread for more information.</a></em> <br /><br />Betty Smith (AKA Sophina Elisabeth Wehner): Born- December 15, 1896; Died- January 17, 1972<br /><br />Born in Brooklyn, New York to German immigrants, she grew up poor in Williamsburg, Brooklyn. These experiences served as the framework to her first novel, A Tree Grows in Brooklyn (19</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10891537771033427862"><em>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name. <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/44217-master-list-of-author-disambiguation-by-spaces">See this thread for more information.</a></em> <br /><br />Betty Smith (AKA Sophina Elisabeth Wehner): Born- December 15, 1896; Died- January 17, 1972<br /><br />Born in Brooklyn, New York to German immigrants, she grew up poor in Williamsburg, Brooklyn. These experiences served as the framework to her first novel, A Tree Grows in Brooklyn (1943).<br /><br />After marrying George H. E. Smith, a fellow Brooklynite, she moved with him to Ann Arbor, Michigan, where he pursued a law degree at the University of Michigan. At this time, she gave birth to two girls and waited until they were in school so she could complete her higher education. Although Smith had not finished high school, the university allowed her to enroll in classes. There she honed her skills in journalism, literature, writing, and drama, winning a prestigious Hopwood Award. She was a student in the classes of Professor Kenneth Thorpe Rowe.<br /><br />In 1938 she divorced her husband and moved to Chapel Hill, North Carolina. There she married Joseph Jones in 1943, the same year in which A Tree Grows in Brooklyn was published. She teamed with George Abbott to write the book for the 1951 musical adaptation of the same name. Throughout her life, Smith worked as a dramatist, receiving many awards and fellowships including the Rockefeller Fellowship and the Dramatists Guild Fellowship for her work in drama. Her other novels include Tomorrow Will Be Better (1947), Maggie-Now (1958) and Joy in the Morning (1963). </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10891537771033427862">...more</a>

    </div>
